  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 12:40:20 UTC)

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 12:40:43 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack

- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.

  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration

- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.

- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 13:06:40 UTC)



---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 13:08:02 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 14:51:10 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack

- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.

  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.

- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.

  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration

  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 17:44:11 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack

## 2. Models & Configuration

- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.

- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 18:16:48 UTC)



---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 18:17:09 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions

- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 18:47:23 UTC)



---

### Agent (Sun, 12 Apr 2026 18:47:43 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.

---

# AgentIRC Project Memory and Architecture Insights

## 1. Core Architecture & Stack
- **Frameworks:** The project relies heavily on **Microsoft AutoGen 0.4+** for orchestrating multi-agent collaboration and **Chainlit** for the web-based chat user interface.
- **Runtime Environment:** The project specifically aims to operate on **Python 3.14.3** (experimental). This requires extreme care around `asyncio` and `anyio` patches (`run.py` and `app.py`) to prevent breaking compatibility with Chainlit and AutoGen's background task management.
- **Split Domain Logic:** The architecture deliberately separates concerns:
  - `simulator_core.py` acts as the pure helper and state layer containing domain logic (history, telemetry, room config).
  - `app.py` acts as the UI gateway, mapping Chainlit event hooks (`@cl.on_message`, `@cl.on_chat_start`) to the simulator core and instantiating the AutoGen agents.

## 2. Models & Configuration
- **Model Registration:** Instead of hardcoding AI specifications, models are registered via an external `agents_config.json`. This config allows dynamic addition of models (like Claude, Gemini, GPT, or arbitrary OpenRouter aliases).
- **Global Provider Details:** API settings, specifically OpenRouter integration, are decoupled into `config.toml`, allowing dynamic updates to the `base_url` and `api_key_env`.
- **System Prompting:** Agents are instantiated in `app.py` (via `create_team`). The prompts are strictly tuned to enforce genuine model personalities (reading from `agents_config.json`) rather than instructing them to act as "fake" simulated IRC users.
- **Multimodal capabilities:** The application is built to handle Vision. Chainlit file uploads containing images are captured in `handle_message`, parsed via `autogen_core.Image.from_file()`, and wrapped into a multimodal array to pass to standard models alongside text.

## 3. Tool Ecosystem (Plugins)
- Tools are centralized in `simulator_tools.py` and mapped via `TOOL_CATALOG`.
- Agents can access utility functions directly. Recent additions include MCP-style web actions:
  - `web_search`: Uses the `duckduckgo_search` library.
  - `fetch_webpage`: Fetches HTML using `requests` and converts it down to context-friendly plain markdown using `markdownify` to protect agent context limits.

## 4. UI / UX Design
- **90s IRC Aesthetic:** The UI is purely styled using custom CSS overrides (`public/style.css`), removing modern elements (avatars, rounded corners) and applying Courier/Terminal monospace fonts.
- **IRC Mechanics:** The system maps standard Chainlit inputs to IRC concepts (`/topic`, `/mode`, `/slap`, `/nick`).
- **Targeting Agents:** Direct messaging (`@AgentName`) limits the broadcast so specific agents can be isolated from the general RoundRobin loop.

## 5. Bridging & Data Persistence
- **State Management:** Session configurations, rooms, and chat histories are maintained in-memory during a session but backed persistently by `simulator_state.json`.
- **Bridges:** The project contains infrastructure (`bridge_runtime.py`, `irc_bridge_runtime.py`, `websocket_bridge_runtime.py`) to externalize the conversation payload into an `outbox/` queue, allowing future external clients or separate platforms to mirror the chat.
- **Leaderboards & Telemetry:** Built-in hooks intercept token usage, message counts, and response latency to display live analytics and "cost" estimations for the operator.

## 6. Documentation Conventions
The repository relies heavily on segmented documentation logic to control agents across sessions:
- **`VISION.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `TODO.md`**: Guide high-level feature direction.
- **`MEMORY.md`**: For technical caveats (like asyncio incompatibilities).
- **`CHANGELOG.md` & `VERSION` file**: Strict version tracking. Every feature addition necessitates an update to the changelog and incrementing the text-only VERSION file.
- **`[LLM].md` (e.g., `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`)**: Contextual instructions specifically designed for human developers or autonomous AI agents taking over the project to maintain consistency across handoffs.
